<div class="elementor-widget-container">
<h2 class="elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default">Meet the author</h2>				</div>
</div>
<div class="elementor-element elementor-element-a024318 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor" data-id="a024318" data-element_type="widget" data-widget_type="text-editor.default">
<div class="elementor-widget-container">
<p>I am Ketki, the writer of this blog. Explore with Ecokats is a sustainable travel blog for travellers seeking information and experiences in destinations all over the world.</p><p>When I am not teaching in the local university or helping NGOs with their environmental publications and training programmes, I travel and then I write. I am a contributor to most India based in-flight magazines and online publications.</p><p>The stories on this blog cover city guides, heritage sites, architectural wonders, national parks and many more with a sustainable dash to it.</p>								</div>

<span class="sbi-screenreader">Kenya Jewellery 😍
I was completely struck by the </span>
<svg class="svg-inline--fa fa-clone fa-w-16 sbi_lightbox_carousel_icon" aria-hidden="true" aria-label="Clone" data-fa-proƒcessed="" data-prefix="far" data-icon="clone" role="img" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 512 512">
<path fill="currentColor" d="M464 0H144c-26.51 0-48 21.49-48 48v48H48c-26.51 0-48 21.49-48 48v320c0 26.51 21.49 48 48 48h320c26.51 0 48-21.49 48-48v-48h48c26.51 0 48-21.49 48-48V48c0-26.51-21.49-48-48-48zM362 464H54a6 6 0 0 1-6-6V150a6 6 0 0 1 6-6h42v224c0 26.51 21.49 48 48 48h224v42a6 6 0 0 1-6 6zm96-96H150a6 6 0 0 1-6-6V54a6 6 0 0 1 6-6h308a6 6 0 0 1 6 6v308a6 6 0 0 1-6 6z"></path>
</svg>						<img decoding="async" src="https://www.explorewithecokats.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed/img/placeholder.png" alt="Kenya Jewellery 😍
I was completely struck by the colourful beadwork in Kenya! And the jewellery is much beyond just an accessory.
In Maasai culture, beads are used to signify age, social status, and major life events like engagements and weddings, and each colour carries its own symbolism — from bravery and strength in red to purity and health in white, and warmth and hospitality in orange. 
The jewellery is handcrafted by women who carry on a craft passed down through generations, and every necklace or bracelet tells a story of community, connection to the landscape, and cultural pride. Proudly adorned by women and men, it is worn everyday and not only on special occasions! 
That’s why taking home a piece of beadwork jewellery feels so much more meaningful than a typical keepsake. 
The jewellery has evolved from head gears, necklace and bracelets to belts, keychains, anklets, earrings footwear and purses to suit the modern travelers! 
Which one would you pick?
Thank you @salliefab for letting me borrow your neck piece for this photo ❤️

<span class="sbi-screenreader">The Giants of Africa
In Amboseli National Park, e</span>
<svg style="color: rgba(255,255,255,1)" class="svg-inline--fa fa-play fa-w-14 sbi_playbtn" aria-label="Play" aria-hidden="true" data-fa-processed="" data-prefix="fa" data-icon="play" role="presentation" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 448 512"><path fill="currentColor" d="M424.4 214.7L72.4 6.6C43.8-10.3 0 6.1 0 47.9V464c0 37.5 40.7 60.1 72.4 41.3l352-208c31.4-18.5 31.5-64.1 0-82.6z"></path></svg>			<img decoding="async" src="https://www.explorewithecokats.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed/img/placeholder.png" alt="The Giants of Africa
In Amboseli National Park, elephants don’t just pass through the landscape, they are the landscape: Unhurried. Unbothered. Ancient.
With Mount Kilimanjaro rising quietly in the background, these herds walk as if the land belongs to them, because it does. Every step feels deliberate, every pause timeless, perfectly framed against a horizon that has witnessed them for generations. 
Watching them across the wetlands, grasslands, lakes while the mountain being the constant backdrop was extremely panoramic and due to that Amboseli Reserve is my favourite national park in Kenya, hands down! 
On a media trip with @global_destinations_rep @indigo.6e and @sopa_lodges 
Have you seen African Elephants?

<span class="sbi-screenreader">Banaras wrapped itself around me and how!
I wande</span>
<svg class="svg-inline--fa fa-clone fa-w-16 sbi_lightbox_carousel_icon" aria-hidden="true" aria-label="Clone" data-fa-proƒcessed="" data-prefix="far" data-icon="clone" role="img" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 512 512">
<path fill="currentColor" d="M464 0H144c-26.51 0-48 21.49-48 48v48H48c-26.51 0-48 21.49-48 48v320c0 26.51 21.49 48 48 48h320c26.51 0 48-21.49 48-48v-48h48c26.51 0 48-21.49 48-48V48c0-26.51-21.49-48-48-48zM362 464H54a6 6 0 0 1-6-6V150a6 6 0 0 1 6-6h42v224c0 26.51 21.49 48 48 48h224v42a6 6 0 0 1-6 6zm96-96H150a6 6 0 0 1-6-6V54a6 6 0 0 1 6-6h308a6 6 0 0 1 6 6v308a6 6 0 0 1-6 6z"></path>
</svg>						<img decoding="async" src="https://www.explorewithecokats.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed/img/placeholder.png" alt="Banaras wrapped itself around me and how!
I wandered through its ancient lanes, letting the city feed me like an old friend — the kind who somehow knows exactly what your heart has been craving.
The first burst of joy was tamatar chaat - warm, sour and chaotic, a perfect introduction to a city that loves with intensity. Then came chooda matar, a gentle winter hug in a bowl — the kind of comfort that makes you slow down without even realising it. 
In those labyrinth lanes, I tasted its edible heritage — the GI-tagged Tirangi Barfi and Lal Peda, sweets that feel less like desserts and more like stories preserved in sugar, nostalgia and pride.
A humble Baati Chokha thali grounded me, reminding me of home in the most unexpected way - food cooked over woodfire, chutneys made over silbatta and flour grounded over a hand mill. Then came Malaiyo (saffron milk foam).. the fleeting winter miracle — light as breath, gone in a second, but unforgettable in the way only Banaras can be.
Somewhere along the way, I found myself sipping thick lassi, hajmola chai (yes, it’s a thing and super yum), crunching into hot chai–toast, and ending my wanderings with a ritualistic Banarasi paan — the perfect full stop to every food chapter.
Banaras didn’t just feed me, it reminded me that some cities aren’t just seen — they’re tasted, felt, remembered. I can go back to Banaras in a heartbeat just for the food. 
Thank you @banaraslanes for taking me to these amazing treasure troves and @juhi_jain1507 @the_yodelers for feeding my soul in Banaras. 
#BanarasFood #VaranasiFood #KashiFoodTrail #BanarasEats #gitag

</a>

{

{

document.getElementById("wpcp-error-message").innerHTML = smessage_text;

}
